EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

EWM Global Strategic Assessment

Phase 2 Consolidated Analysis

1. Business Overview

Company Snapshot

EWM Global is a specialized fintech company providing executive compensation administration services to institutional clients, primarily in the financial services and private equity sectors.

| Attribute | Current State | |:----------|:-------------| | Annual Revenue | $24 million | | Years in Operation | 24 years | | Employees | 170 across 3 locations | | Market Share | 10% of addressable market | | Primary Services | Deferred Cash Plans (69%), Carry/Coinvestment (30%), Share Plans (1%) | | Key Competitors | GPx, HRSoft, Computershare |

Current Position

EWM Global occupies an unusual strategic position: the company has built world-class customer economics but has failed to scale its market presence. After 24 years of operation, 98% customer retention, and $1 million average customer lifetime value, the company holds only 10% market shareâ€”a clear signal that internal constraints, not market limitations, are suppressing growth.

``` â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•— â•‘ CURRENT STATE PARADOX â•‘ â• â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•£ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ EXCEPTIONAL FOUNDATIONS BUT SEVERE CONSTRAINTS â•‘ â•‘ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â•‘ â•‘ 98% Customer Retention â—„â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 10% Close Rate â•‘ â•‘ $1M Customer Lifetime Value â—„â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 0.43 Cash Ratio â•‘ â•‘ 5/5 IT Infrastructure â—„â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 50% Equipment Utilization â•‘ â•‘ 18.5:1 LTV:CAC Ratio â—„â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 270-Day Sales Cycle â•‘ â•‘ $282K Revenue per Employee â—„â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 2/5 Culture Score â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ INTERPRETATION: The company knows how to deliver exceptional value to â•‘ â•‘ customers but cannot efficiently acquire new customers or scale operations â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• ```

2. Key Findings

The comprehensive Phase 2 analysis identified five critical insights that explain EWM Global's current position and define the path forward:

Finding 1: Governance Is the Root Constraint

The absence of external governance enables all other problems to persist.

EWM Global operates without an advisory board and with minimal board oversight (rated 2/5), despite 24 years of operation and $24M in revenue. This governance void creates strategic blind spots, delays critical decisions, and removes the accountability that would force action on known issues like cash management, margin improvement, and sales efficiency.

> "Without external accountability, internal issues remain internal."

Finding 2: Financial Position Cannot Support Growth Ambitions

The company's 20% growth target is mathematically impossible given current capital structure.

| Growth Requirement | Current Capacity | Gap | |:-------------------|:-----------------|:----| | CAC investment needed for 20% growth | $3.7 million | â€” | | Available working capital | $1.5 million | $2.2M shortfall | | Cash ratio (benchmark: 1.2) | 0.43 | 64% below benchmark | | Gross margin (benchmark: 42%) | 32% | 10 points below |

Without external capital, maximum sustainable growth is 12-15%â€”well below stated targets.

Finding 3: Sales Conversion Is the Primary Revenue Leak

90% of sales effort produces zero revenue due to a 10% close rate.

The company's sales velocity index of 25.93 (versus 68 benchmark) indicates fundamental sales process dysfunction. Combined with a 270-day sales cycle, this means:

  • Each lost deal represents $70,000 in potential revenue
  • Approximately $1.5-2.5 million in annual revenue goes unrealized
  • Competitive differentiation clarity at 3/5 prevents effective value articulation

Finding 4: Organizational Dysfunction Undermines Execution

Culture (2/5) and decision-making (2/5) scores indicate an organization unable to execute change.

With only 4 executives managing 170 employees across 3 locations (1:42.5 ratio versus 1:25 best practice), the organization suffers from:

  • Decision bottlenecks that extend sales cycles and response times
  • Cultural fragmentation across locations
  • Change resistance that blocks technology adoption
  • Employee compliance without commitment (3/5 engagement)

Finding 5: Massive Technology Investment Produces Subpar Returns

$2.5M annual technology spend (10.4% of revenue) yields 50% equipment utilization and 3/5 automation.

The company has built infrastructure for 2-3x its current scale but directed technology investment toward client products rather than internal operations. This creates a "cobbler's children" problem where innovation culture (4/5) benefits customers but not internal efficiency.

Dimension-by-Dimension Assessment

| Dimension | Score | Status | Interpretation | |:----------|:-----:|:------:|:---------------| | Customer Economics | 84/100 | â—â—â—â—â—‹ | Exceptionalâ€”market-leading retention and LTV | | Technology Foundation | 84/100 | â—â—â—â—â—‹ | Excellent infrastructure, underutilized | | Compliance Posture | 76/100 | â—â—â—â—‹â—‹ | Strong awareness, monitoring gaps | | Operational Reliability | 70/100 | â—â—â—â—‹â—‹ | High reliability, low efficiency | | Market Position | 64/100 | â—â—â—â—‹â—‹ | Stable but stagnant share | | Operational Efficiency | 56/100 | â—â—â—‹â—‹â—‹ | Significant improvement potential | | People & Culture | 48/100 | â—â—â—‹â—‹â—‹ | Cultural weakness threatens scale | | Financial Health | 44/100 | â—â—‹â—‹â—‹â—‹ | Criticalâ€”primary growth constraint | | Governance Structure | 38/100 | â—â—‹â—‹â—‹â—‹ | Criticalâ€”enables all other issues |

Health Score Interpretation

Score of 61 indicates: The business is fundamentally sound but operating significantly below potential. Strengths are concentrated in customer-facing dimensions (retention, reliability, technology) while weaknesses cluster in internal operations (governance, finance, culture). This asymmetry creates a business that excels at keeping customers but struggles to acquire them or scale efficiently.

Prognosis without intervention: Continued 12-15% growth, gradual competitive erosion, increasing difficulty attracting talent, and diminishing strategic optionality.

Prognosis with transformation: 20%+ growth achievable, market share expansion from 10% to 15%+, and full strategic optionality (continued growth, acquisition, or exit) preserved.

4. Critical Priorities

Top 5 Priorities Requiring Immediate Executive Attention

Priority 1: Secure Growth Capital Facility

Timeline: 0-90 days | Investment: $50-100K preparation | Outcome: $3-5M facility

| Why Critical | Impact if Delayed | |:-------------|:------------------| | Current cash ratio (0.43) cannot fund growth investments | Growth ceiling locked at 12-15% | | 270-day sales cycle requires sustained CAC investment | Competitors gain market share | | Strong customer economics provide excellent collateral | Strategic options narrow |

Immediate Actions:

  1. Prepare 3-year financial projections with sensitivity analysis
  2. Document contracted revenue base and retention metrics
  3. Engage 5-7 fintech-focused lenders within 30 days
  4. Target facility close within 90 days
---

Priority 2: Establish Advisory Board

Timeline: 0-90 days | Investment: $75-100K annually | Outcome: External accountability

| Why Critical | Impact if Delayed | |:-------------|:------------------| | No external strategic guidance despite 24-year operation | Known problems continue unaddressed | | Decision-making effectiveness at 2/5 | Strategic opportunities missed | | Exit/growth strategy requires experienced advisors | Valuation discount in transaction |

Immediate Actions:

  1. Define advisory charter and competency requirements
  2. Target 3-5 advisors: fintech operations, culture/HR, finance, PE expertise
  3. Leverage CEO network and executive search
  4. Commit first 1-2 advisors within 90 days
---

Priority 3: Implement Decision-Making Framework

Timeline: 0-90 days | Investment: $25-50K | Outcome: 40% faster decisions

| Why Critical | Impact if Delayed | |:-------------|:------------------| | 4 executives for 170 employees creates systematic bottlenecks | Continued slow response times | | Decision delays extend sales cycles | Employee frustration and turnover | | Blocks operational improvements | Change initiatives stall |

Immediate Actions:

  1. Audit current decision patterns and bottlenecks
  2. Develop RACI framework with clear authority delegation
  3. Define decision SLAs by category (2 hours to 15 days)
  4. Train managers and launch within 60 days
---

Priority 4: Launch Sales Conversion Transformation

Timeline: 0-6 months | Investment: $150-250K | Outcome: Close rate 10%â†’18%

| Why Critical | Impact if Delayed | |:-------------|:------------------| | 10% close rate wastes 90% of sales investment | $1.5-2.5M annual revenue unrealized | | Competitive differentiation unclear (3/5) | Deals lost to competitors | | Each 5-point improvement = ~$1.5M revenue | Growth target unachievable |

Immediate Actions:

  1. Complete win/loss analysis on 40 recent opportunities
  2. Develop competitive battle cards for top 3 competitors
  3. Implement stage-gate qualification to kill poor deals faster
  4. Train sales team on differentiation messaging
---

Priority 5: Remediate Customer Response Time

Timeline: 0-3 months | Investment: $90-140K | Outcome: 24-hourâ†’8-hour response

| Why Critical | Impact if Delayed | |:-------------|:------------------| | 24-hour response threatens 98% retention ($23.5M at risk) | Customer churn increases | | IT infrastructure (5/5) existsâ€”process is constraint | Investment already made | | Quick win demonstrates improvement capability | Employee confidence in transformation |

Immediate Actions:

  1. Implement automated acknowledgment system (Week 2)
  2. Define tiered SLAs by issue severity
  3. Build knowledge base for top 20 recurring issues
  4. Achieve 12-hour average by Month 3, 8-hour by Month 6

Opportunity Prioritization Rationale

Why Sales Conversion First: The company generates sufficient pipeline but converts only 10%. Improving conversion is the highest-ROI investment because it requires no additional customer acquisition spendingâ€”just better conversion of existing opportunities.

Why Pricing Second: With 98% retention and $1M LTV, customers clearly value the service. The 18.5:1 LTV:CAC ratio (versus 6:1 benchmark) suggests significant pricing headroom. Each 1% price increase flows directly to gross profit ($240K+).

Why Technology Activation Now: The $2.5M annual technology investment already exists. Activation requires adoption and process change, not additional capitalâ€”making it high-return with relatively low incremental investment.

7. Recommended Path Forward

Transformation Roadmap Summary

The recommended approach is a phased 18-month transformation that addresses root causes before symptoms, building capability systematically while generating returns to fund continued investment.

Final Assessment

The Core Insight

EWM Global is not a company in crisisâ€”it is a company constrained below its potential. The foundations are exceptional: 98% customer retention, $1 million lifetime value, industry-leading technology infrastructure, and 24 years of domain expertise. These are not easily replicated and represent genuine competitive advantages.

The constraintsâ€”governance voids, financial limitations, organizational dysfunctionâ€”are all addressable through disciplined execution of the recommended transformation. Unlike market-related or product-related challenges, these are internal execution gaps that leadership can directly control.

The Choice

Option A: Status Quo

  • Growth constrained to 12-15%
  • Competitive position gradually erodes
  • Strategic options (exit, acquisition, continued growth) narrow
  • Exceptional customer economics eventually undermined
Option B: Transformation
  • 20%+ growth achieved and sustainable
  • Market share expands from 10% to 15%+
  • Full strategic optionality preserved
  • Enterprise value increases significantly

Recommendation

Proceed with full transformation immediately.

The investment of $1.8M-$2.5M over 18 monthsâ€”representing 6-8% of revenueâ€”is justified by:

  • 180-280% expected ROI
  • ~11 month payback period
  • Protection of $23.5M+ in retention revenue
  • Creation of $4.5-7M in annual value
  • Preservation of strategic optionality worth 0.5-1.0x EBITDA multiple improvement
The window for action is now. Each month of delay compounds constraints, allows competitors to gain ground, and reduces the options available to leadership. The path forward is clear; the only remaining decision is commitment to execute.

Revenue Engine Analysis: EWM Global

Executive Summary

EWM Global demonstrates a high-value, relationship-driven revenue model with exceptional customer retention and strong unit economics. However, the company faces significant friction in its customer acquisition process, with an extremely long sales cycle and below-benchmark close rates that constrain growth velocity. The 5-percentage-point gap between historical growth (15%) and target growth (20%) will require strategic intervention in sales efficiency and marketing effectiveness.

5. Recommendations

Priority 1: Sales Efficiency Transformation

Closing Assessment

EWM Global possesses a fundamentally strong revenue engine characterized by exceptional customer retention, high-value transactions, and solid unit economics. The company's 24-year operating history and $1M customer lifetime value demonstrate sustained value creation capability.

However, achieving the 20% growth target (versus 15% historical) requires addressing the sales conversion bottleneck. The combination of a 10% close rate and 270-day sales cycle creates friction that constrains revenue velocity despite the high deal values.

The single highest-impact initiative is improving close rates. A 5-percentage-point improvement from 10% to 15% would generate approximately $1.5M - $2.5M in additional annual revenue without requiring proportionally more leads or marketing spend.

Secondary priorities around response time, competitive differentiation, and funnel optimization will create compounding improvements across the revenue engine, positioning EWM Global to achieveâ€”and potentially exceedâ€”its 20% growth objective.

Operational Excellence Analysis: EWM Global

Executive Summary

EWM Global demonstrates a bifurcated operational profile: exceptional technical infrastructure and reliability paired with moderate process efficiency and underutilized assets. As a 24-year fintech company serving financial services with plan administration services, the company has built robust foundational systems but has yet to fully optimize operational throughput and resource utilization. The organization operates above median in most areas but shows significant room for improvement in translating strong infrastructure investments into operational velocity.

By addressing these gaps, EWM Global can transform from a reliable but moderately efficient operation to one that demonstrates operational excellence at scaleâ€”critical for achieving its 20% growth target and potential exit strategy execution.

Financial Health & Strategic Position

Financial Strategic Analysis: EWM Global

Executive Summary

EWM Global presents a paradoxical financial profile: strong customer economics and revenue planning capabilities are undermined by concerning liquidity constraints and below-market profitability. While the company demonstrates excellent customer lifetime value ($1M) and exceptional retention (98%), its 32% gross profit margin and cash ratio of 0.43 reveal significant structural financial vulnerabilities that threaten the company's 20% growth ambitions and long-term strategic optionality.

---

1. Current State Assessment

Revenue Performance & Trajectory

| Metric | Current Value | Context | |--------|--------------|---------| | Annual Revenue | $24M (LY) â†’ $26M (Projected) | 8.3% growth trajectory | | Reported Sales Growth | 15% YoY | Healthy organic growth | | Target Growth | 20% | Aggressive but achievable | | Revenue per Employee | $141,176 | Below industry median |

The company demonstrates solid revenue momentum in a specialized fintech niche. The 5-point growth gap between last year's 15% achievement and this year's 20% target represents an incremental $1.2M in revenue capture requiredâ€”achievable given the high repeat customer rate but challenging given the 270-day sales cycle for new business.

Profitability Analysis

| Metric | Value | Benchmark P50 | Position | |--------|-------|---------------|----------| | Gross Profit Margin | 32% | 42% | Below P10 | | Monthly EBITDA (Est.) | $640,000 | â€” | ~32% operating margin | | Annual Implied Profit | $7.68M | â€” | Strong if accurate |

Critical Finding: The 32% gross profit margin is alarmingly low for a fintech/SaaS company, where industry norms typically range from 60-80%. This suggests either:

  • High cost of service delivery (labor-intensive operations)
  • Suboptimal pricing relative to value delivered
  • High platform/infrastructure costs not yet amortized across sufficient client base
  • Potential categorization of expenses that should be below gross profit line

Liquidity & Cash Position

| Metric | Value | Benchmark P50 | Status | |--------|-------|---------------|--------| | Cash Available | $1,500,000 | â€” | Constrained | | Working Capital | $1,500,000 | â€” | Tight | | Cash Ratio | 0.43 | 1.20 | Critical: Below P10 | | Cash Runway | Not Calculated | 6 months | Data Gap | | Financial Resilience (Self-Rated) | 2/5 | â€” | Limited |

The cash position represents the most significant financial risk. At $1.5M available cash:

  • This represents only 5.8% of annual revenue
  • Less than 2.5 months of estimated monthly profit ($640K)
  • Insufficient buffer for the 270-day sales cycle investment required
  • Minimal cushion for growth investments or unexpected challenges

| Metric | Value | Benchmark | Observation | |--------|-------|-----------|-------------| | Total Debt/Liabilities | Not Disclosed | â€” | Transparency Gap | | Debt-to-Asset Ratio | 0.00 | â€” | Potentially underleveraged | | Debt Monitoring | 3/5 | P50: 3 | At benchmark |

Despite the liquidity challenges, EWM Global demonstrates above-average financial planning and management capabilitiesâ€”suggesting the issues are structural rather than operational.

---

3. Key Strengths

Strength 1: Exceptional Customer Economics & Retention

Evidence:
  • LTV of $1,000,000 per customer
  • CAC:LTV ratio of 18.5x (benchmark P90 is 12x)
  • 98% repeat customer rate (benchmark median is 40%)
  • 69% of revenue from Deferred Cash Plan Administration indicates sticky, recurring relationships
Strategic Implication: The customer economics provide a strong foundation for predictable revenue growth and justify investments in customer success and expansion.

Strength 2: Financial Planning & Forecasting Maturity

Evidence:
  • Cash flow forecasting rated 4/5 (P75 vs. benchmark)
  • Budgeting effectiveness rated 4/5 (P75 vs. benchmark)
  • Growth funding readiness rated 4/5 (P75 vs. benchmark)
  • Sales targets aligned with business needs rated 5/5
Strategic Implication: The company has the financial management infrastructure to execute complex growth initiativesâ€”the challenge is access to capital, not capability to deploy it.

Strength 3: Strategic Clarity on Growth/Exit Path

Evidence:
  • Documented growth/exit plan rated 4/5 (benchmark P90 is 4)
  • Business goals documentation rated 4/5
  • 24-year operating history provides track record
  • Strategic intent clearly defined as "Strategic Growth"
Strategic Implication: Strong strategic documentation positions the company well for potential capital raising, strategic partnerships, or future M&A activity.

Strength 4: Revenue Diversification Potential

Evidence:
  • Three distinct service lines with varying growth profiles
  • Carry/Coinvestment administration (30% of revenue) growing with private equity market
  • Share Plan Administration (1%) represents untapped expansion opportunity
  • 70% of revenue attributed to innovation pipeline
Strategic Implication: Multiple revenue streams reduce concentration risk and provide optionality for strategic emphasis shifts.

---

4. Critical Gaps

Gap 1: Severely Constrained Liquidity (CRITICAL)

Evidence:
  • Cash ratio of 0.43 vs. benchmark P50 of 1.20
  • Self-rated financial resilience of 2/5 ("Limited")
  • $1.5M cash represents only 5.8% of revenue
  • Working capital identical to cash position suggests limited cushion
Risk Quantification:
  • 270-day sales cycle requires ~$54,000 CAC investment per new customer
  • To achieve 20% growth (~$5.2M new revenue), need approximately 74 new customers at $70K average
  • Total CAC investment required: ~$4M over sales cycle
  • Current cash position: $1.5M (37.5% of required investment)
Impact: Cash constraints will likely:
  1. Force slower new customer acquisition than growth targets require
  2. Limit ability to invest in sales and marketing expansion
  3. Create vulnerability to unexpected expenses or revenue timing variations
  4. Reduce negotiating leverage in any capital discussions

Gap 2: Below-Market Gross Profit Margin

Evidence:
  • 32% GPM vs. 42% benchmark median (24% relative underperformance)
  • Below P10 of industry (28%)
  • SaaS/fintech norms are 60-80%
Root Cause Analysis: | Possible Cause | Likelihood | Evidence | |----------------|------------|----------| | High service delivery costs | High | 81 support/admin vs. 4 executives | | Underpricing relative to value | Medium | $70K average deal but $1M LTV suggests room | | Technology amortization pressure | Medium | $2.5M annual tech investment | | Competitive pricing pressure | Medium | 10% market share, growing competitor position |

Impact: Every 1% GPM improvement translates to ~$240,000 additional gross profit annually, providing significant leverage for both reinvestment and liquidity improvement.

Gap 3: Financial Data Quality & Transparency

Evidence:
  • Total debt/liabilities: Not disclosed
  • Monthly expenses: $3.5M stated (impossible given $24M annual revenue)
  • Monthly burn rate: $4 stated (clearly erroneous)
  • Cash runway: Not calculated
Impact: Data quality issues suggest:
  1. Potential gaps in financial reporting infrastructure
  2. Difficulty in precise financial planning and scenario modeling
  3. Challenges if seeking external capital (due diligence concerns)
  4. Risk of misaligned decision-making based on incomplete data

Gap 4: Working Capital Mismatch with Sales Cycle

Evidence:
  • 270-day sales cycle (above P90 of 75 days)
  • 10% close rate (below P10 of 12%)
  • Working capital of $1.5M must support 9-month sales investments
Cash Conversion Cycle Analysis:
  • Customer acquisition investments made at Day 0
  • Revenue recognition begins at Day 270+
  • Cash collection potentially Day 300-330
  • Negative working capital requirement of ~$200K per new customer during cycle
Impact: The combination of long sales cycles, low close rates, and limited working capital creates a cash flow timing trap that will constrain growth without external financing.

Gap 5: Revenue Per Employee Below Benchmark

Evidence:
  • $141,176 revenue per employee vs. $160,000 benchmark median
  • 12% productivity gap
  • 170 total workforce for $24M revenue
Impact: Lower revenue per employee indicates:
  1. Potential for operational efficiency improvements
  2. May reflect labor-intensive service delivery model
  3. Contributes to margin compression
  4. Limits ability to fund competitive compensation
---

5. Strategic Recommendations

Immediate Priorities (0-6 Months)

Recommendation 1: Secure Credit Facility
Action: Establish a $3-5M revolving credit facility or line of credit secured against receivables or contracted revenue.

Rationale:

  • Current 0.43 cash ratio is unsustainable for growth ambitions
  • Strong customer retention (98%) and contracted revenue provide collateral value
  • Credit facility provides flexibility without equity dilution
Financial Impact:
  • Cost: Prime + 2-3% (~$150-225K annual interest at full utilization)
  • Benefit: Enables full execution of growth plan worth $5.2M incremental revenue
Implementation:
  1. Prepare 3-year financial projections with sensitivity analysis
  2. Document contracted revenue and customer concentration
  3. Approach 3-5 lenders including fintech-focused banks
  4. Target close within 90 days
Recommendation 2: Conduct Gross Margin Deep Dive
Action: Engage finance and operations in detailed analysis of cost structure to identify margin improvement opportunities.

Analysis Framework: | Category | Investigation Focus | |----------|---------------------| | Service Delivery | Labor costs, automation potential, process efficiency | | Technology | Cloud costs, licensing, build vs. buy decisions | | Pricing | Value-based pricing analysis, competitive benchmarking | | Customer Mix | Margin by customer segment and service line |

Target: Identify path to 40% GPM within 18 months (8-point improvement = $1.9M additional gross profit)

Recommendation 3: Clean Up Financial Data & Reporting
Action: Implement standardized financial reporting with accurate monthly metrics.

Specific Fixes Required:

  • Reconcile monthly expense data (current $3.5M figure is incorrect)
  • Document total debt and liability position
  • Calculate accurate cash runway
  • Implement monthly cash flow tracking
Investment: CFO time + potential fractional controller support (~$50-75K annually)

Medium-Term Priorities (6-18 Months)

Recommendation 4: Optimize Pricing Strategy
Action: Implement value-based pricing review across all service lines.

Opportunity Analysis: | Service Line | Revenue % | Margin Assessment | Pricing Opportunity | |--------------|-----------|-------------------|---------------------| | Deferred Cash Plan Admin | 69% | Likely highest | 5-10% increase feasible | | Carry/Coinvestment | 30% | Growing demand | Premium pricing potential | | Share Plan | 1% | Low volume | Needs strategic review |

Target: 3-5% average price increase = $720K-$1.2M additional revenue at near-100% margin flow-through

Recommendation 5: Establish Customer Payment Terms Optimization
Action: Review and optimize customer payment terms to improve cash conversion.

Strategies:

  • Implement annual prepay discounts (5% discount for annual upfront payment)
  • Introduce quarterly billing for applicable services
  • Evaluate milestone-based billing for implementation phases
Impact: Even 30-day improvement in collections on existing revenue = ~$2M working capital improvement

Recommendation 6: Develop Financial Contingency Planning
Action: Given self-rated financial resilience of 2/5, create formal contingency plans.

Components:

  1. Identify $1-2M in discretionary spending that could be deferred if needed
  2. Establish trigger points for cost containment measures
  3. Create scenario models for revenue shortfall scenarios (10%, 20%, 30% miss)
  4. Document potential asset monetization options

Long-Term Strategic Priorities (18+ Months)

Recommendation 7: Evaluate Strategic Capital Options
Action: Given strong customer economics and strategic growth intent, evaluate growth capital options.

Options Analysis: | Option | Pros | Cons | Fit for EWM | |--------|------|------|-------------| | Growth Equity | Non-dilutive to founders, board expertise | Higher cost of capital, covenants | Strong | | Strategic Investment | Customer access, market validation | Potential competition conflicts | Moderate | | Bank Term Loan | Lower cost, no dilution | Requires collateral, conservative sizing | Moderate | | Revenue-Based Financing | Flexible repayment, fast close | Higher effective rate, revenue dependence | Moderate |

Recommendation: Given documented exit/growth plan (4/5), growth equity or strategic investment likely best aligned with long-term objectives.

Recommendation 8: Build Toward 40%+ Gross Margins
Long-Term Margin Improvement Roadmap:

| Timeframe | Target GPM | Key Levers | |-----------|------------|------------| | Current | 32% | Baseline | | Year 1 | 36% | Pricing optimization, operational efficiency | | Year 2 | 40% | Automation, customer mix optimization | | Year 3 | 45% | Scale benefits, technology leverage |

Investment Required:

  • Process automation initiatives: $500K-1M
  • Platform scalability improvements: Included in current $2.5M tech budget
  • Pricing infrastructure: $100-200K
Return Potential: 13-point margin improvement on $30M+ revenue = $3.9M+ additional gross profit

Conclusion

EWM Global's financial position reveals a company with exceptional unit economics and customer relationships constrained by structural profitability challenges and liquidity limitations. The 98% retention rate and $1M LTV validate the business model, but 32% gross margins and a 0.43 cash ratio create real constraints on executing the 20% growth target.

The central financial paradox: The company rates its growth funding readiness at 4/5, yet self-rates financial resilience at 2/5. This disconnect suggests leadership recognizes the strategic soundness of the business model while acknowledging the tactical cash constraints.

Priority Actions:

  1. Immediate: Secure $3-5M credit facility to provide growth capital and liquidity cushion
  2. Near-term: Conduct gross margin deep-dive to identify path to 40%+ GPM
  3. Medium-term: Optimize pricing and payment terms to improve both margins and cash conversion
  4. Long-term: Position for strategic capital raise aligned with documented exit/growth objectives
The strong customer economics and recurring revenue characteristics make EWM Global an attractive candidate for growth capitalâ€”the key is addressing the liquidity constraints before they force suboptimal strategic decisions.

3. Key Strengths

ğŸŸ¢ Strength 1: Operational Workforce Productivity

Score: Revenue per Employee >P90

EWM Global's workforce generates $282,353 per full-time employeeâ€”exceeding even the 90th percentile benchmark of $280,000. This indicates:

  • Deep domain expertise in fintech administration
  • Effective leverage of technology investments ($2.5M annually)
  • Strong operational workflows (documentation rated 4/5)
  • Mature, specialized workforce developed over 24 years
Strategic Implication: The company has built institutional knowledge and efficiency that creates competitive advantage. Protecting this through retention strategies is critical.

ğŸŸ¢ Strength 2: Turnover Below Industry Average

Score: 19.9% vs. 22% median

Despite cultural challenges, EWM Global retains employees better than most peers:

  • Turnover rate sits between P25 (15%) and P50 (22%)
  • Suggests compensation, job stability, or role satisfaction offsets cultural weaknesses
  • 98% repeat customer rate may provide job meaning and stability
  • Specialized fintech expertise limits external opportunities
Strategic Implication: Employees are staying despite engagement challengesâ€”likely due to compensation or limited alternatives. This creates fragility; addressing root causes of cultural weakness is essential before market dynamics shift.

ğŸŸ¢ Strength 3: Succession Planning Above Median

Score: 3/5 vs. P50 of 2

Leadership succession readiness exceeds industry norms:

  • Documented growth/exit plan (4/5)
  • Some leadership development occurring (3/5)
  • Provides continuity protection for 24-year-old enterprise
Strategic Implication: This strength provides a foundation for building deeper leadership bench strength and governance structures.

ğŸŸ¢ Strength 4: Operational Reliability Supporting Employee Stability

Score: Operations Reliability 5/5

Excellent operational reliability (5/5) creates a stable work environment:

  • Documented workflows (4/5) reduce confusion and conflict
  • High IT infrastructure quality (5/5) minimizes frustration
  • Strong data management (5/5) supports employee effectiveness
Strategic Implication: Technical and operational excellence provides employees with tools to succeed; the gap is in human and leadership systems.

4. Critical Gaps

ğŸ”´ Critical Gap 1: Weak Organizational Culture

Score: 2/5 (Limited) | Industry P50: 3 | Industry Mean: 3.3

This is EWM Global's most pressing people challenge. A "Limited" culture rating indicates:

Root Cause Analysis:

  • 3-location structure may fragment shared identity
  • 24 years of organic growth without intentional culture cultivation
  • Leadership rates culture creation as 3/5 but outcome is 2/5â€”execution gap
  • Moderate engagement (3/5) suggests employees are compliant but not committed
  • High personnel utilization (80%) may drive transactional rather than values-driven work
Business Impact: | Risk Category | Manifestation | |---------------|---------------| | Recruitment | Difficulty attracting top talent who research culture | | Retention | Turnover may spike if market improves for specialists | | Innovation | Innovation culture rated 4/5 but weak culture limits collaboration | | Integration | M&A or rapid hiring will fail without clear cultural identity | | Client Delivery | B2B fintech clients increasingly value vendor culture fit |

Severity: CRITICAL â€” Culture is the foundation; weakness here undermines all other people initiatives.

ğŸ”´ Critical Gap 2: Ineffective Decision-Making

Score: 2/5 (Limited) | Industry P50: 3 | Industry Mean: 3.3

At the 10th percentile or below, decision-making dysfunction creates cascading problems:

Manifestation Patterns:

  • Decision-making structure rated 3/5 but effectiveness only 2/5

  • Limited board oversight (2/5) means no external accountability for decision quality
  • 4 executives for 170 employees may create bottlenecks

ğŸŸ¡ Moderate Gap 5: Engagement-Culture Disconnect

  • Financial resilience rated 2/5â€”employees may sense instability

5. Recommendations

Immediate Priorities (0-6 Months)

1. Establish Governance Foundation
Investment: ~$50-100K annually | Impact: High

| Action | Detail | |--------|--------| | Form Advisory Board | Recruit 3-5 advisors with fintech, HR, and scaling expertise | | Board Charter | Define meeting cadence (quarterly), decision authority, compensation | | Board Composition | Target: 1 fintech operator, 1 HR/culture expert, 1 financial services executive | | Quick Win | Engage advisors on decision-making audit as first project |

Rationale: External perspective will accelerate all other improvements and signal maturity to clients and potential acquirers.

---

2. Decision-Making Architecture Redesign
Investment: Internal + $25-50K external facilitation | Impact: Critical

| Action | Detail | |--------|--------| | Decision Audit | Map current decision processes; identify delays and bottlenecks | | RACI Framework | Implement clear Responsible/Accountable/Consulted/Informed matrices | | Authority Delegation | Push decisions to lowest appropriate level | | Escalation Protocols | Define clear escalation paths and timeframes | | Meeting Structure | Redesign leadership meetings around decision-making rather than reporting |

Success Metrics:

  • Average decision time reduction of 40%
  • Decision-making effectiveness score improvement to 3/5 within 12 months
  • Employee satisfaction with decision clarity (survey baseline and target)
---

3. Cultural Diagnostic & Foundation Work
Investment: $30-75K diagnostic + internal effort | Impact: Foundational

| Action | Detail | |--------|--------| | Cultural Assessment | Deploy comprehensive survey across all 3 locations | | Focus Groups | Conduct confidential sessions by level and location | | Values Articulation | If undefined, engage employees in values discovery | | Leadership Alignment | Executive team workshop on culture ownership | | Communication | Share findings and commitment to change transparently |

Key Questions to Answer:

  • What does "weak culture" specifically mean at EWM Global?
  • Is culture fragmented by location, tenure, or function?
  • What elements of culture do employees value vs. want changed?
---

Target Outcome: Ready bench of 6-8 leaders prepared for expanded roles as company grows.

Key Metric: Move employee engagement from 3/5 to 4/5 within 18 months.

Conclusion

EWM Global possesses strong operational fundamentalsâ€”evident in industry-leading productivity metrics, below-average turnover, and excellent technical infrastructure. However, the People & Leadership dimension represents a structural constraint on the organization's strategic aspirations.

The combination of weak culture, ineffective decision-making, and absent governance creates compounding risk:

  • Culture shapes engagement shapes retention shapes productivity
  • Decision-making speed determines competitive positioning in fintech
  • Governance gaps limit strategic optionality and client confidence
The 20% growth target and documented exit strategy are at risk without foundational improvements. The recommended investment of ~1.5-2.5% of revenue in Year 1 is modest relative to the strategic stakes and positions EWM Global to translate its operational excellence into sustainable organizational capability.

The core message: EWM Global has built a strong engine (operations, technology, customer relationships) but lacks the driver infrastructure (culture, leadership, governance) to navigate the next phase of growth. Addressing this imbalance is not optionalâ€”it is prerequisite to strategic execution.

---

Conclusion

EWM Global has established a solid compliance foundation that positions it well for its role as a fintech provider to financial services companies. The company's excellent regulatory awareness, strong incident reporting, and outstanding technology infrastructure provide significant competitive advantages.

However, critical gaps in financial resilience and governance create sustainability risks that could undermine the compliance program over time. The company's below-average gross margins and limited cash position constrain its ability to invest in compliance improvements and respond to regulatory changes.

Priority Focus Areas:

  1. Financial resilience improvement â€“ Address the 64% cash ratio gap as an urgent priority
  2. Governance enhancement â€“ Establish advisory board and strengthen oversight
  3. Compliance monitoring upgrade â€“ Close the gap between awareness and active monitoring
  4. Margin improvement â€“ Create sustainable funding for ongoing compliance investment
With targeted investments of $850K-$1.3M over 18 months and disciplined execution of the recommended roadmap, EWM Global can achieve a compliance sustainability score improvement of approximately 17%, positioning the company for sustainable growth while maintaining regulatory excellence.

This asymmetry explains why, after 24 years, EWM Global holds only 10% market share despite world-class customer economics.

The Cash Arithmetic: ``` â•”â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•— â•‘ THE GROWTH FUNDING GAP â•‘ â• â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•£ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ 20% Growth Target = $4.8M Additional Revenue â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ Customers Required: 69 new customers at $70K average â•‘ â•‘ CAC Investment: $54,000 Ã— 69 = $3,726,000 â•‘ â•‘ Sales Cycle: 270 days (cash tied up 9 months) â•‘ â•‘ Close Rate Reality: At 10%, need 690 opportunities â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ AVAILABLE: $1,500,000 â•‘ â•‘ REQUIRED: $3,726,000 (minimum) â•‘ â•‘ GAP: $2,226,000 (60% shortfall) â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ CONCLUSION: The business model requires capital intensity that current â•‘ â•‘ financial position cannot support â•‘ â•‘ â•‘ â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• ```

The Technology Paradox Equation: ``` TECHNOLOGY EFFICIENCY ANALYSIS â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• INPUT OUTPUT â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ $2.5M Tech Investment Operational Efficiency: 60% 5/5 IT Infrastructure â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º Equipment Utilization: 50% 5/5 Data Management Automation: 3/5 10.4% of Revenue Response Time: 24 hours â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• EXPECTED CORRELATION: P90 investment â†’ P90 outcomes ACTUAL CORRELATION: P90 investment â†’ P25-P50 outcomes ROOT CAUSE IDENTIFIED: Technology built for clients, not operations Innovation directed externally (70% revenue) Internal adoption blocked by governance/culture ```

3. Contradictions & Tensions

The Paradox Map

EWM Global's profile contains six fundamental contradictions that create internal friction and strategic confusion:

``` CONTRADICTION MATRIX â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

STRENGTH CONTRADICTION WEAKNESS â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ PARADOX 1: High Tech Investment BUT Low Operational $2.5M (>P90) â—„â”€â”€â–º Efficiency (3/5) PARADOX 2: Excellent Retention BUT Poor Acquisition 98% (>P99) â—„â”€â”€â–º 10% close (<P10) PARADOX 3: Strong Planning BUT Weak Execution 4/5 Documentation â—„â”€â”€â–º 2/5 Decisions PARADOX 4: Financial Expertise BUT Financial Fragility 4/5 Forecasting â—„â”€â”€â–º 0.43 Cash Ratio PARADOX 5: Culture Creation Intent BUT Culture Reality 3/5 Leadership Effort â—„â”€â”€â–º 2/5 Outcome PARADOX 6: External Innovation BUT Internal Stagnation 70% Revenue from Innovation â—„â”€â”€â–º 3/5 Automation

â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•ï¿½ï¿½ï¿½â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• ```

Paradox 1: Technology Investment vs. Operational Output

The Tension:

  • Investment: $2.5M annual technology spend (10.4% of revenue, >P90)
  • Output: 60% operational efficiency, 50% equipment utilization, 24-hour response time
Why This Contradiction Exists: ``` TECHNOLOGY INVESTMENT FLOW ANALYSIS Where the $2.5M Goes: What It Produces: â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ CLIENT PRODUCTS â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 70% of revenue from innovation âœ“ â”œâ”€â”€ Plan administration platform â”œâ”€â”€ Carry/coinvestment systems â””â”€â”€ Share plan technology INFRASTRUCTURE â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 5/5 IT capability âœ“ â”œâ”€â”€ Data centers/cloud â”œâ”€â”€ Network systems â””â”€â”€ Security INTERNAL OPERATIONS â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 3/5 automation âœ— â”œâ”€â”€ Process automation â”œâ”€â”€ Support systems NOT PRIORITIZED â””â”€â”€ Internal tools CONCLUSION: Technology investment is externally-focused (products) not internally-focused (operations) ```

Strategic Implication: The company builds excellent technology for clients but doesn't apply the same capability to its own operationsâ€”a classic "cobbler's children" problem.

Paradox 2: Retention Excellence vs. Acquisition Dysfunction

The Tension:

  • Retention: 98% repeat rate (>P99), $1M LTV
  • Acquisition: 10% close rate (<P10), 270-day cycle
Why This Contradiction Exists: ``` THE ACQUISITION-RETENTION ASYMMETRY BEFORE SALE AFTER SALE â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ Differentiation: 3/5 (unclear) â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º 5/5 (proven) Value Proposition: Theoretical â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º Demonstrated Relationship: Transactional â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º Partnership Switching Costs: Zero â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º Very High â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• DIAGNOSIS: The company cannot articulate its value BEFORE the sale but consistently proves it AFTER the sale This explains: â”œâ”€â”€ 10% close rate (struggle to convince prospects) â”œâ”€â”€ 98% retention (customers see value once implemented) â”œâ”€â”€ 270-day cycle (takes time to prove value during sales process) â””â”€â”€ 10% market share (can't scale acquisition despite excellence) ```

Strategic Implication: EWM Global's competitive differentiation clarity (3/5) is the bridge between its acquisition weakness and retention strengthâ€”improving this alone could dramatically improve sales conversion.

  • Execution: 2/5 decision-making, 270-day sales cycle, 24-hour response time
Why This Contradiction Exists: ``` PLANNING vs. EXECUTION GAP The company KNOWS what to do: But CANNOT execute: â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ âœ“ 20% growth target identified âœ— Cash constraints block investment âœ“ Exit strategy documented âœ— Governance gaps prevent action âœ“ Financial forecasts prepared âœ— Decision-making effectiveness 2/5 âœ“ Goals clearly articulated âœ— Leadership capacity insufficient â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•ï¿½ï¿½â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â• ROOT CAUSE: Planning is an individual/small team activity Execution requires organizational capacity The 4 executives can PLAN at high levels but cannot EXECUTE through 170 employees without better governance and decision structures ```

Systemic Issue 1: Founder-Stage Governance in Growth-Stage Company

The Root Cause:

After 24 years and $24M in revenue, EWM Global exhibits governance structures more typical of a 5-year, $5M startup:

| Governance Element | EWM Global | Typical for $24M Company | |:-------------------|:-----------|:-------------------------| | Advisory Board | None | 3-5 advisors | | Board Oversight | 2/5 | 3.5-4/5 | | Independent Directors | Unknown | 1-2 minimum | | Executive Committee | 4 people | 6-8 people | | Decision Authority | Centralized | Distributed |

Multi-Dimensional Manifestation:

| Dimension | How Governance Gap Manifests | |:----------|:-----------------------------| | Revenue | No push to address 10% close rate | | Operations | No accountability for efficiency | | Financial | No pressure to secure capital or improve margins | | People | Culture deteriorates without oversight | | Compliance | Potential blind spots | | Growth | Strategic execution slow | | Market | Competitive adaptation delayed | | Resources | Decision gridlock traps resources | | Risk | No external risk perspective | | Scalability | Organizational constraints unaddressed |

Why This Persists:

  • Without external accountability, internal issues remain internal
  • Founders may not recognize governance gaps (don't know what they don't know)
  • Short-term operational focus crowds out structural improvements
  • No forcing function for governance investment
---

Systemic Issue 2: Reliability-Over-Efficiency Operating Philosophy

The Root Cause:

The company has culturally prioritized zero-failure over throughput optimization, creating redundancy-heavy operations.

``` RELIABILITY vs. EFFICIENCY TRADE-OFF ANALYSIS â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

RELIABILITY EFFICIENCY â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ Current Score: 5/5 3/5 This creates: â”œâ”€â”€ Redundant systems (higher cost) â”œâ”€â”€ Over-provisioned capacity (50% utilization) â”œâ”€â”€ Conservative processes (slower throughput) â”œâ”€â”€ Manual verification (lower automation) â””â”€â”€ Risk-averse culture (change resistance)

â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

OPTIMAL BALANCE FOR FINTECH:

Industry Best Practice: 4/5 Reliability + 4/5 Efficiency EWM Global Current: 5/5 Reliability + 3/5 Efficiency Gap: Over-indexed on reliability by 1 point Under-indexed on efficiency by 1 point COST OF IMBALANCE: â”œâ”€â”€ 32% GPM vs 42% benchmark (partially explained) â”œâ”€â”€ $2.5M tech spend producing 50% utilization â”œâ”€â”€ Process bottlenecks despite excellent infrastructure â””â”€â”€ Innovation resources directed to redundancy, not improvement ```

Why This Persists:

  • Financial services clients expect zero-failure
  • 24-year track record of reliability creates institutional memory
  • "If it ain't broke, don't fix it" culture
  • Efficiency improvements feel risky to reliability-focused culture
---

Systemic Issue 3: Cash-Growth Spiral

The Root Cause:

A self-reinforcing negative cycle where low margins create low cash, limiting investment, constraining growth, and perpetuating low margins.

``` THE CASH-GROWTH SPIRAL â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ LOW MARGINS â”‚ â”‚ (32% GPM) â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â”‚ â”‚ LOW CASH â”‚ â”‚ ($1.5M, 0.43 ratio) â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â”‚ â”‚ LIMITED INVESTMENT â”‚ â”‚ (Cannot fund sales, automation, leadership) â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â”‚ â”‚ SLOW GROWTH â”‚ â”‚ (15% vs 20% target) â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â”‚ â”‚ LIMITED SCALE BENEFITS â”‚ â”‚ (Cannot amortize fixed costs) â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â”‚ â”‚ CONTINUED LOW MARGINS â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

BREAKING THE SPIRAL REQUIRES EXTERNAL INTERVENTION: â”œâ”€â”€ Credit facility injection breaks cash constraint â”œâ”€â”€ Pricing optimization breaks margin constraint â”œâ”€â”€ Sales efficiency breaks growth constraint â””â”€â”€ All three together reverse the spiral ```

Why This Persists:

  • Governance gap prevents external capital discussions
  • Decision-making delays margin improvement initiatives
  • Culture prioritizes reliability over efficiency (margin impact)
  • No forcing function to break the cycle
---

Systemic Issue 4: Acquisition Model Mismatch

The Root Cause:

EWM Global's business model requires sustained capital intensity that its financial structure cannot support.

``` BUSINESS MODEL vs. FINANCIAL STRUCTURE MISMATCH â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

BUSINESS MODEL REQUIREMENTS: FINANCIAL STRUCTURE REALITY: â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

$54,000 CAC per customer $1,500,000 available cash 270-day sales cycle Limited working capital 10% close rate (690 opportunities No credit facility needed for 69 wins) 32% GPM limits cash generation

MATH: â”œâ”€â”€ To achieve 20% growth: Need 69 new customers â”œâ”€â”€ At $54K CAC: Need $3.7M in pipeline investment â”œâ”€â”€ At 270-day cycle: Cash tied up for 9 months â”œâ”€â”€ Available: $1.5M â””â”€â”€ GAP: $2.2M minimum

â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

THE MISMATCH: EWM Global has built an enterprise B2B model requiring significant working capital intensity, but has not secured the capital structure to support that model at growth rates above 12-15% ```

Why This Persists:

  • The 98% retention masks the acquisition inefficiency
  • Historical 15% growth was achievable within constraints
  • 20% growth target exposes the structural mismatch
  • No governance push to address capital structure
---

Systemic Issue 5: Build-Without-Adopt Technology Pattern

The Root Cause:

The company excels at building technology for clients but systematically fails to adopt technology for internal operations.

``` BUILD vs. ADOPT ANALYSIS â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

CLIENT TECHNOLOGY INTERNAL TECHNOLOGY â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€ Investment: HIGH HIGH Focus: Products Infrastructure Adoption: Strong (70% rev) Weak (3/5 automation) Improvement: Continuous Stagnant

â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WHY THE DIFFERENCE?

CLIENT TECHNOLOGY: â”œâ”€â”€ Revenue directly tied to innovation â”œâ”€â”€ Customer demand creates urgency â”œâ”€â”€ Competitive pressure forces action â”œâ”€â”€ Clear measurement of success â””â”€â”€ External accountability

INTERNAL TECHNOLOGY: â”œâ”€â”€ No direct revenue attribution â”œâ”€â”€ No customer demanding internal efficiency â”œâ”€â”€ Reliability culture resists change â”œâ”€â”€ Success harder to measure â”œâ”€â”€ No external accountability â””â”€â”€ 2/5 decision-making delays adoption

THE PATTERN: Build (easy, visible) â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º Deploy (requires change management) â”€â”€â”€â”€â–º FAIL â”‚ â–¼ Culture (2/5) blocks adoption Decisions (2/5) delay rollout Reliability focus resists change ```

Why This Persists:

  • External innovation has clear revenue attribution
  • Internal innovation requires organizational change capability the company lacks
  • Governance gap means no accountability for technology ROI
  • Culture prioritizes stability over optimization
---

Leverage Point 1: Governance Establishment (HIGHEST LEVERAGE)

Why This Is The Primary Leverage Point:

Governance touches every other dimension because it creates the accountability and decision-making structure to address all other issues.

``` GOVERNANCE CASCADE EFFECT â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

GOVERNANCE ESTABLISHMENT (Advisory Board + Decision Framework) â”‚ â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â–¼ â–¼ FINANCIAL OPERATIONAL CULTURAL ACCOUNTABILITY ACCOUNTABILITY ACCOUNTABILITY â”‚ â”‚ â”‚ â–¼ â–¼ â–¼ â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â” â”‚â€¢ Credit â”‚ â”‚â€¢ Response â”‚ â”‚â€¢ Culture â”‚ â”‚ facility â”‚ â”‚ time fix â”‚ â”‚ initiativeâ”‚ â”‚â€¢ Margin â”‚ â”‚â€¢ Automationâ”‚ â”‚â€¢ Decision â”‚ â”‚ improve â”‚ â”‚ adoption â”‚ â”‚ rights â”‚ â”‚â€¢ Pricing â”‚ â”‚â€¢ Equipmentâ”‚ â”‚â€¢ Leadershipâ”‚ â”‚ strategy â”‚ â”‚ utilizationâ”‚ â”‚ developmentâ”‚ â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜ â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜ â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

WITHOUT GOVERNANCE: Each issue remains siloed, unaccountable, unaddressed WITH GOVERNANCE: External pressure + decision velocity enables all improvements ```

Expected Multi-Dimensional Impact:

| Dimension | How Governance Improves It | |:----------|:---------------------------| | Financial | External accountability forces credit facility, margin improvement | | Operations | Decision velocity enables process changes | | People | Leadership development becomes priority | | Compliance | Oversight ensures proactive monitoring | | Growth | Strategic decisions accelerate | | Market | Competitive positioning clarified | | Resources | Decision gridlock resolved | | Risk | External perspective on vulnerabilities | | Scalability | Organizational constraints addressed |

Investment & Return:

  • Investment: $100-150K annually (advisory board, governance structure)
  • Return: Enables $2-4M in improvements across other dimensions
  • ROI: 400-600% by unlocking other initiatives
---

Leverage Point 2: Capital Access (IMMEDIATE NECESSITY)

Why This Is Critical:

Every growth initiative requires investment that current cash position cannot support.

``` CAPITAL ACCESS UNLOCK CHAIN â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

$3-5M CREDIT FACILITY â”‚ â–¼ 8. Conclusion: The Integrated View

EWM Global's Fundamental Situation

The cross-dimensional analysis reveals EWM Global as a company with world-class customer retention trapped behind founder-stage governance and financial constraints. The business has proven it can deliver exceptional value to customersâ€”98% retention, $1M LTV, 18.5:1 LTV:CAC ratioâ€”but cannot efficiently acquire new customers or scale operations to capture its market potential.

The Path Forward

EWM Global's transformation requires addressing root causes (governance, capital, decision-making) before symptoms (sales conversion, response time, efficiency). The cross-dimensional analysis demonstrates that many apparent individual problems are manifestations of fewer systemic issues.

The investment of $1.3-2.4M over 18 months can unlock:

  • Revenue growth from 15% to 20%+
  • Gross margin improvement from 32% to 38%
  • Market share trajectory from 10% toward 15-20%
  • Organizational health from 3.04/5 to 4.0/5
Without intervention:
  • Growth will stagnate at 12-15%
  • Competitive position will erode
  • Key personnel departures become likely
  • Strategic optionality (exit, growth, sale) diminishes

Final Assessment

EWM Global is not a company in crisisâ€”it is a company constrained below its potential. The strengths are real and valuable. The customer economics are exceptional. The technology is superior. The domain expertise is deep.

The transformation required is not about building new capabilities from scratchâ€”it is about removing the governance, financial, and organizational barriers that prevent existing strengths from being fully leveraged.

The choice is clear: Invest in structural transformation and unlock substantial value, or continue with current constraints and watch potential erode over time.

Executive Summary

Based on the comprehensive analysis of EWM Global across all ten Phase 1 dimensions, this report presents 15 prioritized strategic recommendations designed to address critical gaps, leverage existing strengths, and enable the company to achieve its 20% growth target.

The analysis reveals a company with exceptional foundational assetsâ€”98% customer retention, $1M customer LTV, and industry-leading IT infrastructureâ€”constrained by three interconnected barriers: financial liquidity (cash ratio 0.43), organizational dysfunction (culture and decision-making both at 2/5), and sales conversion inefficiency (10% close rate).

CRITICAL PRIORITY RECOMMENDATIONS

Recommendation 1: Secure Growth Capital Facility

Title

Establish $3-5M Revolving Credit Facility to Enable Growth Investment

Description

EWM Global's current cash position of $1.5M with a cash ratio of 0.43 (64% below the industry benchmark of 1.2) represents the single most significant constraint on growth execution. The company's 270-day sales cycle requires sustained investment in customer acquisition ($54,000 CAC per customer), which cannot be funded from current working capital. To achieve the 20% growth target ($4.8M additional revenue), the company needs approximately 69 new customers, requiring ~$3.7M in acquisition investmentâ€”more than double the available cash.

Securing a credit facility will provide the financial flexibility to invest in sales expansion, operational improvements, and strategic initiatives without depleting operational reserves. The company's exceptional customer retention (98%) and contracted revenue base provide strong collateral for favorable lending terms.

Priority

CRITICAL

Timeframe

Immediate (0-90 days)

Impact Areas

  • Financial Health & Strategic Alignment
  • Revenue Engine & Sales Capacity
  • Growth Readiness
  • Risk & Resilience
  • Scalability & Infrastructure

Dependencies

  • Clean financial data and accurate reporting (address data quality issues first)
  • 3-year financial projections with sensitivity analysis
  • Documentation of contracted revenue and customer concentration
  • CEO/CFO alignment on capital structure strategy

Expected Outcomes

| Metric | Current State | Target State | Timeline | |:-------|:--------------|:-------------|:---------| | Cash Ratio | 0.43 | 0.90+ | 90 days | | Available Working Capital | $1.5M | $4.5-6.5M | 90 days | | Sales Pipeline Funding Capacity | 28 concurrent pursuits | 80+ concurrent pursuits | 120 days | | Growth Investment Capacity | Constrained | Fully funded | 90 days |

Implementation Steps

``` PHASE 1: PREPARATION (Weeks 1-4) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 1: Engage fractional controller to clean financial data â”œâ”€â”€ Week 2: Prepare historical financial statements and projections â”œâ”€â”€ Week 3: Document contracted revenue base and retention metrics â””â”€â”€ Week 4: Complete lending package with customer concentration analysis

PHASE 2: OUTREACH (Weeks 5-8) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 5: Identify 5-7 fintech-friendly lenders and specialty banks â”œâ”€â”€ Week 6: Submit initial inquiries and term sheet requests â”œâ”€â”€ Week 7: Conduct lender presentations and facility structure discussions â””â”€â”€ Week 8: Receive and evaluate initial term sheets

PHASE 3: NEGOTIATION & CLOSE (Weeks 9-12) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 9: Select preferred lender(s) and negotiate key terms â”œâ”€â”€ Week 10: Legal review and documentation preparation â”œâ”€â”€ Week 11: Final due diligence and covenant negotiation â””â”€â”€ Week 12: Execute facility agreement and initial draw ```

Investment Required: $50-100K (legal, advisory, preparation fees) Annual Cost: $150-250K (interest at prime + 2-3% on average utilization) Value Unlocked: Enables $3-5M in growth investments; removes primary scaling constraint

Recommendation 2: Establish Strategic Advisory Board

Title

Form Advisory Board to Address Governance Gaps and Accelerate Strategic Decision-Making

Description

EWM Global operates without external governance structures despite 24 years of operation and $24M in revenue. The absence of an advisory board, combined with board oversight rated at 2/5 and decision-making effectiveness at 2/5, creates strategic blind spots and decision bottlenecks that cascade across all business functions. The current 4-executive structure for 170 employees (1:42.5 ratio) is insufficient for the complexity of a growth-stage fintech company.

An advisory board will provide external expertise, accountability, and strategic guidance while accelerating decision-making through experienced perspectives. Given the documented exit/growth strategy (rated 4/5), advisory board members with M&A, capital markets, and fintech scaling experience will be particularly valuable.

Priority

CRITICAL

Timeframe

Immediate (0-90 days for formation; ongoing for operation)

Impact Areas

  • People & Leadership Ecosystem
  • Compliance & Sustainability
  • Financial & Strategic Alignment
  • Growth Readiness
  • Market Position & Competitive Dynamics

Dependencies

  • CEO commitment to external governance and accountability
  • Clarity on advisory board charter and decision-making authority
  • Budget allocation for advisor compensation
  • Identification of strategic priorities for advisor expertise

Expected Outcomes

| Metric | Current State | Target State | Timeline | |:-------|:--------------|:-------------|:---------| | Board/Leadership Oversight | 2/5 | 3.5/5 | 12 months | | Decision-Making Effectiveness | 2/5 | 3/5 | 6 months | | Strategic Review Frequency | 3/5 | 4/5 | 6 months | | External Accountability | None | Quarterly reviews | 90 days |

Implementation Steps

``` PHASE 1: DESIGN (Weeks 1-3) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 1: Define advisory board charter, scope, and decision authority â”œâ”€â”€ Week 2: Identify expertise gaps (fintech operations, M&A, HR/culture, finance) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 3: Develop compensation structure and time commitment expectations

PHASE 2: RECRUITMENT (Weeks 4-8) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 4: Create target advisor profiles and initial candidate list â”œâ”€â”€ Week 5: Leverage existing network and executive search for candidates â”œâ”€â”€ Week 6: Conduct introductory conversations with potential advisors â”œâ”€â”€ Week 7: Evaluate candidates against expertise needs and cultural fit â””â”€â”€ Week 8: Extend formal invitations to 3-5 selected advisors

PHASE 3: ACTIVATION (Weeks 9-12) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 9: Onboard advisors with company overview and strategic context â”œâ”€â”€ Week 10: Establish meeting cadence and communication protocols â”œâ”€â”€ Week 11: Conduct first advisory board meeting with strategic priorities â””â”€â”€ Week 12: Assign initial advisory workstreams (e.g., governance, growth strategy) ```

Recommendation 3: Redesign Decision-Making Architecture

Title

Implement Decision Rights Framework to Eliminate Executive Bottlenecks

Description

EWM Global's decision-making effectiveness rating of 2/5 (below the 10th percentile) creates cascading delays across the organization. With only 4 executives managing 170 employees across 3 locations, decision bottlenecks manifest as 270-day sales cycles, 24-hour customer response times, and slow adaptation to competitive pressures. The current structure forces routine operational decisions through executive approval, consuming leadership bandwidth needed for strategic priorities.

A formal decision rights framework (RACI) will establish clear authority levels, enabling faster execution while preserving appropriate oversight for strategic decisions. This foundation is essential for the organizational scalability required to achieve 20% growth.

Priority

CRITICAL

Timeframe

Immediate (0-90 days for framework; ongoing refinement)

Impact Areas

  • People & Leadership Ecosystem
  • Operational Excellence
  • Revenue Engine (sales velocity)
  • Customer Experience (response time)
  • Scalability & Infrastructure

Dependencies

  • Executive team commitment to delegation
  • Clear role definitions across the organization
  • Middle management capability assessment
  • Communication and change management planning

Expected Outcomes

| Metric | Current State | Target State | Timeline | |:-------|:--------------|:-------------|:---------| | Decision-Making Effectiveness | 2/5 | 3.5/5 | 12 months | | Average Decision Latency | 5-10 days | 2-3 days | 6 months | | Executive Strategic Time | ~30% | ~60% | 6 months | | Employee Decision Satisfaction | Not measured | >70% positive | 12 months |

Implementation Steps

``` PHASE 1: ASSESSMENT (Weeks 1-3) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 1: Audit current decision patterns across departments â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Catalog recurring decisions by type, frequency, and current approver â”œâ”€â”€ Week 2: Identify bottlenecks and authority gaps â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Interview managers on decision frustrations and delays â””â”€â”€ Week 3: Benchmark decision authority levels against similar-stage companies

PHASE 2: DESIGN (Weeks 4-6) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 4: Create decision categorization framework â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Strategic, Tactical, Operational, Routine â”œâ”€â”€ Week 5: Develop RACI matrix for each decision category â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Define Responsible, Accountable, Consulted, Informed roles â””â”€â”€ Week 6: Establish escalation protocols and SLAs by decision type

PHASE 3: IMPLEMENTATION (Weeks 7-12) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 7: Present framework to leadership and gather feedback â”œâ”€â”€ Week 8: Communicate changes to all employees with training â”œâ”€â”€ Week 9: Launch pilot in one department/location â”œâ”€â”€ Week 10: Gather feedback and refine based on pilot learnings â”œâ”€â”€ Week 11: Roll out across organization with monitoring â””â”€â”€ Week 12: Establish ongoing decision effectiveness measurement ```

Investment Required: $25-50K (external facilitation, documentation, training) Ongoing Cost: Minimal (measurement and refinement) Value Created: 40% reduction in decision latency, executive bandwidth recovery, faster sales cycles

Recommendation 4: Launch Sales Conversion Transformation Program

Title

Systematically Improve Close Rate from 10% to 18% Through Sales Efficiency Optimization

Description

EWM Global's 10% close rate (below the 10th percentile versus the 25% benchmark) represents the most significant revenue leakage in the business. Combined with the 270-day sales cycle, this inefficiency means 90% of sales effort produces no revenue, and the company requires 9 months of investment for each successful customer acquisition. The root causes appear to be unclear competitive differentiation (3/5), inadequate sales enablement, and poor pipeline qualification.

This transformation program will systematically identify and address the specific factors causing deal losses, implement rigorous pipeline qualification, and equip the sales team with tools to articulate competitive differentiation. Each 5-percentage-point improvement in close rate generates approximately $1.5-2.5M in additional annual revenue with the same pipeline investment.

Priority

CRITICAL

Timeframe

Short-term (0-6 months for initial improvements; 12 months for full transformation)

Impact Areas

  • Revenue Engine Analysis
  • Financial & Strategic Alignment
  • Growth Readiness
  • Market Position & Competitive Dynamics
  • Resource Optimization

Dependencies

  • Historical sales data availability for win/loss analysis
  • Sales team engagement and willingness to change
  • Competitive intelligence gathering
  • Decision-making framework implementation (Recommendation 3)

Expected Outcomes

| Metric | Current State | Target State | Timeline | |:-------|:--------------|:-------------|:---------| | Close Rate | 10% | 15% (Year 1), 18% (Year 2) | 12-24 months | | Sales Cycle Length | 270 days | 220 days (Year 1), 200 days (Year 2) | 12-24 months | | Sales Velocity Index | 25.93 | 50+ | 12 months | | Additional Annual Revenue | â€” | $1.5-2.5M | 12 months |

Implementation Steps

``` PHASE 1: DIAGNOSTIC (Weeks 1-6) â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 1-2: Win/Loss Analysis â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Conduct structured interviews on 20 recent wins â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Conduct structured interviews on 20 recent losses â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Identify top 5 deal-breaking factors â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 3-4: Pipeline Analysis â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Map conversion rates by pipeline stage â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Identify stages with highest drop-off â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Analyze deal characteristics of wins vs. losses â””â”€â”€ Weeks 5-6: Competitive Positioning Assessment â”œâ”€â”€ Deep-dive on GPx, HRSoft, Computershare offerings â”œâ”€â”€ Interview top 10 customers on "Why EWM?" â””â”€â”€ Document differentiation gaps

PHASE 2: ENABLEMENT (Weeks 7-14) â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 7-8: Develop Updated Sales Tools â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Competitive battle cards with objection handling â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ ROI calculator for prospect conversations â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Customer reference program materials â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 9-10: Pipeline Qualification Criteria â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Implement lead scoring model â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Define stage-gate criteria for progression â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Create disqualification protocols â””â”€â”€ Weeks 11-14: Sales Team Training â”œâ”€â”€ Differentiation messaging role-playing â”œâ”€â”€ Qualification discipline coaching â””â”€â”€ Deal acceleration techniques

HIGH PRIORITY RECOMMENDATIONS

Recommendation 5: Customer Response Time Remediation

Title

Description

EWM Global's 24-hour average customer response time (below the 10th percentile versus the 4-hour benchmark) creates a significant vulnerability to the company's exceptional 98% retention rate, which protects $23.5M in annual recurring revenue. This gap is particularly inconsistent with the company's 5/5 IT infrastructure rating, suggesting process and resource allocation issues rather than technical limitations.

For enterprise fintech clients managing complex compensation plans, slow response times signal service quality concerns that can influence renewal decisions and referrals. Given the $1M customer LTV, even a 1% increase in churn would result in ~$240K annual revenue loss.

HIGH

Timeframe

  • Customer Experience
  • Revenue Engine (retention)
  • Risk & Resilience
  • Compliance & Sustainability

Dependencies

  • Customer tier classification
  • IT/automation resources for implementation
  • Decision framework (for escalation protocols)

Implementation Steps

``` PHASE 1: QUICK WINS (Weeks 1-4) â”œâ”€â”€ Week 1: Implement automated acknowledgment system â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Immediate auto-response with ticket number and SLA â”œâ”€â”€ Week 2: Define tiered response SLA by issue severity â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Critical (system down): 1-hour response â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ High (functionality blocked): 4-hour response â”‚ â”œâ”€â”€ Medium (degraded service): 8-hour response â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Low (questions/requests): 24-hour response â”œâ”€â”€ Week 3: Create customer tier prioritization â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Premium clients receive expedited routing â””â”€â”€ Week 4: Establish escalation protocols with clear ownership

PHASE 2: CAPACITY OPTIMIZATION (Weeks 5-10) â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 5-6: Analyze support ticket volume vs. staffing â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Identify peak periods and coverage gaps â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 7-8: Build knowledge base for Tier 1 resolution â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Document solutions for top 50 recurring issues â””â”€â”€ Weeks 9-10: Implement ticket routing automation â””â”€â”€ Auto-assign based on issue type and team expertise

PHASE 3: SUSTAINED IMPROVEMENT (Weeks 11-26) â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 11-14: Launch response time monitoring dashboard â”‚ â””â”€â”€ Real-time visibility for management â”œâ”€â”€ Weeks 15-20: Cross-train support team for coverage flexibility â””â”€â”€ Weeks 21-26: Implement continuous improvement loop â”œâ”€â”€ Weekly response time reviews â””â”€â”€ Monthly customer feedback integration ```

Recommendation 8: Leadership Capacity Expansion

Title

Description

EWM Global's current structure of 4 executives managing 170 employees (1:42.5 ratio) significantly exceeds healthy span-of-control benchmarks (1:8 to 1:12 for executive leadership). This structural constraint is a root cause of the 2/5 decision-making effectiveness score and contributes to organizational bottlenecks across sales, operations, and customer service.

Adding 2-3 director-level leaders will create a middle management layer that can absorb operational decisions, develop emerging talent, and provide executives with bandwidth for strategic initiatives. This is essential for achieving and sustaining 20% growth.

Priority

HIGH

Timeframe

  • People & Leadership Ecosystem
  • Operational Excellence
  • Scalability & Infrastructure
  • Growth Readiness
  • Risk & Resilience

  • Clear job descriptions and authority delegation
  • Organizational design decisions

Conclusion

EWM Global possesses the foundational strengthsâ€”exceptional customer retention, strong technology infrastructure, and deep domain expertiseâ€”to achieve and sustain its 20% growth ambitions. However, the company is currently constrained by a interconnected set of barriers in financial liquidity, organizational capability, and sales efficiency that must be addressed systematically.

The 15 recommendations presented in this report provide a comprehensive roadmap for transformation, prioritized to address the most critical constraints first while building toward sustainable long-term capability. The total investment of $2.8-4.5M over 24 months represents 5-8% of revenueâ€”a significant but appropriate commitment given the $5.3-8.5M in annual value creation potential and the strategic importance of achieving growth targets.

The key insight: EWM Global's challenges are not market-related or product-relatedâ€”they are execution-related. The company has built a fortress of customer value but lacks the operational and organizational mechanisms to scale it. By implementing these recommendations in priority order, EWM Global can unlock its substantial trapped potential and position itself for sustained growth and strategic optionality.

Recommended immediate actions:

  1. Initiate credit facility discussions this week
  2. Begin advisory board candidate identification
  3. Launch decision audit and RACI development
  4. Commission sales win/loss analysis
The window for action is now. Financial constraints will only tighten without intervention, and organizational challenges compound with growth. A disciplined, phased approach starting with the critical priorities will create momentum and demonstrate results that build confidence for the longer-term initiatives.

Risk Assessment

Comprehensive Risk Assessment

EWM Global

---

Executive Summary

This comprehensive risk assessment consolidates findings from all 10 Phase 1 analyses to identify, prioritize, and provide mitigation strategies for significant risks facing EWM Global. The analysis reveals 27 distinct risk factors across 7 categories, with 5 critical risks requiring immediate intervention and 8 high-priority risks demanding near-term attention.

Conclusion & Prioritized Action Plan

Risk Assessment Summary

EWM Global faces a concentrated cluster of interconnected critical risks that create cascading effects across all business functions. The five critical risksâ€”liquidity crisis, governance void, weak culture, decision-making dysfunction, and sales conversion failureâ€”are not independent; they reinforce each other in ways that amplify overall organizational risk exposure.

The company's exceptional strengths in customer retention (98%), technology infrastructure (5/5), and operational reliability (5/5) provide significant defensive assets. However, these strengths are undermined by foundational weaknesses that, if unaddressed, will constrain growth to 12-15% (vs. 20% target) and create vulnerability to competitive displacement or market shocks.
